manufacturer warranty cost well their ability to comply with vehicle emission standard business continued the california vehicle emission program also includes requirement for manufacturer to produce and deliver for sale zero emission vehicle zevs the current light duty vehicle zev regulation which us system based on credit that can be banked and carried forward mandate substantial annual increase in the production and sale of battery electric fuel cell and plug in hybrid vehicle through the model year at that time the regulation will require credit equating to of manufacturer california light duty vehicle sale volume california is in the process of adopting new zev regulation applicable to model year the proposed regulation include substantial annual increase in required sale volume significant restriction on credit usage and new requirement for ev battery durability california ha also instituted zev regulation aimed at medium and heavy duty vehicle beginning with the model year these medium and heavy duty rule which could entail significant cost and compliance challenge include complex warranty and recall requirement for some vehicle configuration compliance with zev rule depends on market condition well the availability of adequate infrastructure to support vehicle charging european requirement european union eu and regulation directive and related legislation limit the amount of regulated pollutant that may be emitted by new motor vehicle and engine sold in the eu and the united kingdom regulatory stringency ha increased significantly since stage vi emission standard were introduced with the subsequent implementation of laboratory test cycle for and emission and the introduction of on road emission testing using portable emission analyzer real driving emission or rde these on road emission test are in addition to the laboratory based test the divergence the regulatory limit that is tested in laboratory condition and the allowed value measured in rde test will ultimately be reduced to zero the regulatory demand increase in addition new requirement for tailpipe and non tailpipe emission will be included in the upcoming euro regulation the cost associated with complying with all of these requirement are significant and following the eu commission indication of it intent to accelerate emission rule in it road map publication eu green deal well the eu sustainable mobility action plan these challenge will continue in european market including the united kingdom in addition the whole vehicle type approval wvta regulation ha been updated to increase the stringency of in market surveillance moreover following the withdrawal from the european union we may be subject to diverging requirement in our european market which could increase vehicle complexity and duty there is an increasing trend of city access restriction for internal combustion engine powered vehicle particularly in european city that do not meet air quality limit the access rule introduced are developed by individual city based on their specific concern resulting in rapid deployment of access rule that differ greatly among city the speed of implementation of access rule may directly influence customer vehicle residual value and choice of next purchase and there is risk that these rule may result in the need for customer to retrofit their vehicle with emission after treatment system in an effort to support the paris accord some country are adopting yearly increase in tax where such system is in place and publishing date by when internal combustion powered vehicle may no longer be registered norway in and the united kingdom and the netherlands in other national requirement many country in an effort to address air quality and climate change concern are adopting previous version of european or united nation economic commission for europe un ece mobile source emission regulation some country have adopted more advanced regulation based on the most recent version of european or regulation for example the china stage vi light duty vehicle emission standard based on european stage vi emission standard for light duty vehicle evaporative and refueling emission standard and carb obd ii requirement incorporate two level of stringency for tailpipe emission under the level one vi standard which is currently in place nationwide in china the emission limit are comparable to the eu stage vi limit except for co which is lower than the eu stage vi limit the more stringent level two vi standard emission limit are approximately lower than the eu stage vi limit depending on the pollutant while level two vi is not slated for nationwide implementation july the government ha encouraged the more economically developed city and province to pull ahead implementation for example shanghai tianjin hebei province and guangdong province have all begun implementing level two vi both china stage vii light duty vehicle and heavy duty vehicle emission regulation are currently under evaluation and the ministry of ecology and environment ha advised that the stage vii regulation will have more stringent limit on pollutant emission and will establish limit for greenhouse gas primarily tailpipe emission canadian criterion emission regulation are largely aligned with requirement however the existing zev regulation in quebec and those published in british columbia in july are more stringent than those in place in california the federal government ha started preliminary consultation on potential zev mandate elsewhere there is mix of regulation and process based on and eu standard not all country have adopted appropriate fuel quality standard to accompany the stringent emission standard adopted this could lead to compliance problem particularly if obd or in use surveillance requirement are implemented business continued global development in recent year epa and carb have increased their focus on the use of defeat device defeat device are element of design typically embedded in software that improperly cause the emission control system to function le effectively during normal on road driving than during an official laboratory emission test without justification are prohibited by law in many jurisdiction and we do not use defeat device in our vehicle regulator around the world continue to scrutinize automaker emission testing which ha led to number of defeat device settlement by various manufacturer epa is carrying additional non standard test part of it vehicle certification program carb ha also been conducting extensive non standard emission test which in some case have resulted in certification delay for diesel vehicle in the past several european country have conducted non standard emission test and published the result and in some case this supplemental testing ha triggered investigation of manufacturer for possible defeat device testing is expected to continue on an ongoing basis in addition plaintiff attorney are pursuing consumer class action lawsuit based on alleged excessive emission from car and truck which could in turn prompt further investigation by regulator vehicle fuel economy and greenhouse gas standardsu requirement light duty vehicle federal law requires that light duty vehicle meet minimum corporate average fuel economy cafe standard set by the national highway traffic safety administration nhtsa manufacturer are subject to substantial civil penalty if they fail to meet the cafe standard in any model year after taking into account all available credit for the preceding five model year and expected credit for the three succeeding model year the law requires nhtsa to promulgate and enforce separate cafe standard applicable to each manufacturer fleet of domestic passenger car imported passenger car and light duty truck epa also regulates vehicle greenhouse gas ghg emission under the clean air act because the vast majority of ghgs emitted by vehicle are the result of fuel combustion ghg emission standard are similar to fuel economy standard thus nhtsa and epa coordinate with each other on their fuel economy and ghg standard respectively to avoid potential inconsistency beginning with the model year epa and nhtsa jointly promulgated harmonized ghg and fuel economy regulation under came to be known the one national program onp framework california which had promulgated it own state specific set of ghg regulation agreed that compliance with the federal program would satisfy compliance with it own ghg requirement thereby avoiding patchwork of potentially conflicting federal and state ghg standard onp ha required manufacturer to achieve increasingly stringent year over year standard onp wa envisioned to continue at least through the model year in epa introduced significantly le stringent fuel economy and ghg standard applicable to model year the federal government also revoked california authority to set and enforce it own vehicle ghg standard well the authority of other state that opted in to california standard california continued to assert it authority to regulate vehicle ghgs challenged in court the federal government preemption action withdrew from onp and planned to return to enforcing it own state specific ghg standard the litigation over both standard and preemption with uncertain outcome created difficulty for purpose of ford future product planning to avoid bifurcated regulatory scenario in which california and the other state that adopted california ghg standard enforce one set of rule while different set of rule applies in the rest of the country ford reached an agreement with california on set of term for an alternative framework in which ford committed to meet designated set of standard on national basis in lieu of the california regulatory program this framework enabled ford to continue it product planning on nationwide basis while being consistent with ford environmental goal ford finalized it agreement with california in and other state that adopted the california standard indicated they would respect the agreement business continued in epa evaluated the stringency of fuel economy and ghg standard through the model year and whether to restore the stringency to the previous onp level or greater final ghg standard applicable to model year were finalized in december with increased stringency these standard along with more stringent fuel economy standard for model year that are expected to be finalized in could increase cost and complexity for ford the federal government also acted in december to repeal it rule blocking california authority to set and enforce it own vehicle ghg standard well the authority of other state that adopted california standard epa is expected to take similar action in early under the clean air act if any federal or state agency imposes and enforces fuel economy and ghg standard that are misaligned with market condition ford would likely be forced to take various action that could have substantial adverse effect on it sale volume and result of operation such action likely would include restricting offering of selected engine and popular option increasing market support program for ford most fuel efficient vehicle and ultimately curtailing the production and sale of certain vehicle such high performance car utility and or full size light truck in order to maintain compliance requirement heavy duty vehicle epa and nhtsa have jointly promulgated ghg and fuel economy standard for heavy duty vehicle generally vehicle over pound gross vehicle weight rating through the model year in ford case the standard primarily affect heavy duty pickup truck and van plus vocational vehicle such shuttle bus and delivery truck the heavy duty standard increase in stringency it may become more difficult to comply while continuing to offer full lineup of heavy duty truck european requirement the european union operation key trend and economic factor affecting ford and the automotive industrysupplier disruption the automotive industry ha complex supply network with each manufacturer product containing component sourced from supplier who in turn source component from their supplier when there is shortage of key component in our supply chain and the component can not be easily sourced from different supplier the shortage can disrupt production since early we and others in the automotive industry have faced significant shortage of semiconductor the global semiconductor shortage is due in large part to maker of semiconductor having allocated their capacity to meet surging demand for consumer electronics during the covid pandemic while automotive oems experienced industry wide plant closure at the same time wafer foundry that support chipmakers have not invested enough in recent year to increase capacity to the level needed to support demand from all of their customer wafer have long lead time for production which further exacerbates the shortage when global automaker resumed vehicle production in even more quickly than some expected semiconductor supply became further strained combination of these factor including increased demand for consumer electronics automotive shutdown due to covid the rapid recovery of demand for vehicle and long lead time for wafer production is contributing to the ongoing shortage of semiconductor for additional information on the impact of the semiconductor shortage see the outlook section on page covid the impact of covid including change in consumer behavior pandemic fear and market downturn and restriction on business and individual activity ha created significant volatility in the global economy consistent with the action taken by governmental authority in late march we idled our manufacturing operation in region around the world other than china where manufacturing operation were suspended in january and february before beginning to resume operation in march successful phased restart of our manufacturing plant supply network and other dependent function occurred in the second quarter of the remote work arrangement that we implemented in remain in place in most location our remote work arrangement have been designed to allow for continued operation of non production business critical function including financial reporting system and internal control the full impact of covid on future result depends on future development such the ultimate duration and scope of outbreak including any potential future wave due to variant or otherwise and the success of vaccination program and their impact on our customer dealer and supplier despite the successful restart of our manufacturing operation in we continue to experience intermittent covid related disruption in our supply chain moreover new restriction could have an adverse effect on production supply chain distribution and demand for vehicle for additional information on the impact and potential impact of covid on please see item risk factor on page global redesign we previously announced our plan for the global redesign of our business pursuant to monetary policy in response to the covid pandemic the federal reserve and other central bank around the world are poised to withdraw monetary stimulus by raising interest rate the last time the fed shifted from easing to tightening from through the dollar strengthened and financial market became more volatile increased volatility in both developed and emerging market currency may again be result of policy tightening emerging market also face differing inflation backdrop and in some case exposure to commodity price and political instability contributing to unpredictable movement in the value of their exchange rate in addition to direct impact on the financial flow of global automotive company currency movement can also impact pricing of vehicle exported to overseas market most notably in the case of the japanese yen and korean in most market exchange rate are market determined and all are impacted by many different macroeconomic and policy factor and thus likely to remain volatile represents risk to automotive price and revenue pricing pressure over the last year price of both new and used vehicle have increased substantially due to both rising demand and supply shortage it is likely that the rate of price increase will slow auto production slowly recovers from the semiconductor shortage but it is unclear whether price will decline fully to pre covid pandemic level over the long term intense competition and excess capacity are likely to put downward pressure on inflation adjusted price for similarly contented vehicle and contribute to challenging pricing environment for result of operation continued revenueour automotive segment revenue is generated primarily by sale of vehicle part and accessory revenue is recorded when control is transferred to our customer generally our dealer and distributor for the majority of sale this occurs when product are shipped from our manufacturing facility however we defer portion of the consideration received when there is separate future or stand ready performance obligation such extended service contract or ongoing vehicle connectivity revenue related to extended service contract is recognized over the term of the agreement in proportion to the cost we expect to incur in satisfying the contract obligation revenue related to other future or stand ready performance obligation is generally recognized on straight line basis over the period in which service are expected to be performed vehicle sold to daily rental car company with an obligation to repurchase for guaranteed amount exercisable at the option of the customer are accounted for operating lease with lease revenue and profit recognized over the term of the lease proceeds from the sale of vehicle at auction are recognized in revenue upon transfer of control of the vehicle to the buyer most of the vehicle sold by to our dealer and distributor are financed at wholesale by ford credit upon ford credit originating the wholesale receivable related to dealer purchase of vehicle ford credit pay cash to the relevant automotive legal entity in payment of the dealer obligation for the purchase price of the vehicle the dealer then pay the wholesale finance receivable to ford credit when it sell the vehicle to retail customer our ford credit segment revenue is generated primarily from interest on finance receivables net of certain deferred origination cost that are included reduction of financing revenue and such revenue is recognized over the term of the receivable using the interest method also revenue from operating lease is recognized on straight line basis over the term of the lease income is generated to the extent revenue exceed expense most of which are interest depreciation and operating expense transaction between our automotive and ford credit segment occur in the ordinary course of business for example we offer special retail financing and lease incentive to dealer customer who choose to finance or lease our vehicle from ford credit the cost for these incentive is included in our estimate of variable consideration at the date the related vehicle sale to our dealer are recorded in order to compensate ford credit for the lower interest or lease payment offered to the retail customer we pay the discounted value of the incentive directly to ford credit when it originates the retail finance or lease contract with the dealer customer ford credit recognizes the incentive amount over the life of retail finance contract an element of financing revenue and over the life of lease contract reduction to depreciation see note of the note to the financial statement for more detailed discussion of transaction between our automotive and ford credit segment cost and expensesour income statement classifies our company excluding ford credit total cost and expense into two category cost of sale and ii selling administrative and other expense we include within cost of sale those cost related to the development production and distribution of our vehicle part accessory and service specifically we include in cost of sale each of the following material cost including commodity cost freight cost warranty including product recall cost labor and other cost related to the development and production of our vehicle and connectivity part accessory and service depreciation and amortization and other associated cost we include within selling administrative and other expense labor and other cost not directly related to the development and production of our vehicle part accessory and service including such expense advertising and sale promotion cost management discussion and analysis of financial condition and result of operation continued certain of our cost such material cost generally vary directly with change in volume and mix of production in our industry production volume often varies significantly from quarter to quarter and year to year quarterly production volume experience seasonal shift throughout the year including peak retail sale season and the impact on production of model changeover and new product launch annual production volume are heavily impacted by external economic factor including the pace of economic growth and factor such the availability of consumer credit and cost of fuel result we analyze the profit impact of certain cost change holding constant present year volume and mix and currency exchange in order to evaluate our cost trend absent the impact of varying production and currency exchange level we analyze these cost change in the following category contribution cost these cost typically vary with production volume these cost include material including commodity warranty and freight and duty cost structural cost these cost typically do not have directly proportionate relationship to production volume these cost include manufacturing vehicle and software engineering spending related advertising and sale promotion administrative information technology and selling and pension and opeb cost while contribution cost generally vary directly in proportion to production volume element within our structural cost category are impacted to differing degree by change in production volume we also have varying degree of discretion when it come to controlling the different element within our structural cost for example depreciation and amortization expense largely is associated with prior capital spending decision on the other hand while labor cost do not vary directly with production volume manufacturing labor cost may be impacted by change in volume for example when we increase overtime add production shift or add personnel to support volume increase other structural cost such advertising or engineering cost do not necessarily have directly proportionate relationship to production volume our structural cost generally are within our discretion although to varying degree and can be adjusted over time in response to external factor we consider certain structural cost to be direct investment in future growth and revenue for example structural cost are necessary to grow our business and improve profitability invest in new product and technology respond to increasing industry sale volume and grow our market share cost of sale and selling administrative and other expense for full year were billion our automotive segment material and commodity cost make up the largest portion of these cost and expense followed by structural cost although material cost are our largest absolute cost our margin can be affected significantly by change in any category of cost management discussion and analysis of financial condition and result of operation continued result of operation net income attributable to ford motor dealer which generally occurs shortly after being produced in contrast our automotive trade payable are based primarily on industry standard production supplier payment term of about day result our cash flow deteriorates if wholesale volume and the corresponding revenue decrease while trade payable continue to become due conversely our cash flow improves if wholesale volume and the corresponding revenue increase while new trade payable are generally not due for about day for example the suspension of production at most of our assembly plant and lower industry volume due to covid in early resulted in an initial deterioration of our cash flow while the subsequent resumption of manufacturing operation and return to pre covid production level at most of our assembly plant resulted in subsequent improvement of our cash flow even in normal economic condition however these working capital balance generally are subject to seasonal change that can impact cash flow for example we typically experience cash flow timing difference associated with inventory and payable due to our annual summer and december shutdown period when production and therefore inventory and wholesale volume are usually at their lowest level while payable continue to come due and be paid the net impact of this typically result in cash outflow from change in our working capital balance during these consider an accounting estimate to be critical if the accounting estimate requires to make assumption about matter that were highly uncertain at the time the accounting estimate wa made and change in the estimate that are reasonably likely to occur from period to period or use of different estimate that we reasonably could have used in the current period would have material impact on our financial condition or result of operation management ha discussed the development and selection of these critical accounting estimate with the audit committee of our board of director in addition there are other item within our financial statement that require estimation but are not deemed critical defined above change in estimate used in these and other item could have material impact on our financial statement warranty and field service actionsnature of estimate required we provide base warranty on the product we sell for specific period of time and or mileage which vary depending upon the type of product and the geographic location of it sale separately we also periodically perform field service action related to safety recall emission recall and other product campaign pursuant to these warranty and field service action we will repair replace or adjust part on vehicle that are defective in factory supplied material or workmanship we accrue the estimated cost of both base warranty coverage and field service action at the time of sale in addition from time to time we issue extended warranty at our expense the estimated cost of which is accrued at the time of issuance assumption and approach used we establish our estimate of base warranty obligation using patterned estimation model we use historical information regarding the nature frequency and average cost of claim for each vehicle line by model year we reevaluate our estimate of base warranty obligation on regular basis experience ha shown that initial data for any given model year may be volatile therefore our process relies on long term historical average until sufficient data are available with actual experience we use the data to update the historical average we then compare the resulting accrual with present spending rate to ass whether the balance are adequate to meet expected future obligation based on this data we update our estimate necessary field service action may occur in period beyond the base warranty coverage period we establish our estimate of field service action obligation using patterned estimation model we use historical information regarding the nature frequency severity and average cost of claim for each model year we ass our obligation for field service action on regular basis using actual claim experience and update our estimate necessary due to the uncertainty and potential volatility of the factor used in establishing our estimate change in our assumption could materially affect our financial condition and result of operation see note of the note to the financial statement for information regarding warranty and field service action cost pension and other postretirement employee benefit nature of estimate required the estimation of our defined benefit pension assumption and approach used we are subject to the income tax law and regulation of the many jurisdiction in which we operate these tax law and regulation are complex and involve uncertainty in the application to our fact and circumstance that may be open to interpretation we recognize benefit for these uncertain tax position based upon process that requires judgment regarding the technical application of the law regulation and various related judicial opinion if in our judgment it is more likely than not defined likelihood of more than that the uncertain tax position will be settled favorably for we estimate an amount that ultimately will be realized this process is inherently subjective since it requires our assessment of the probability of future outcome we evaluate these uncertain tax position on quarterly basis including consideration of change in fact and circumstance such new regulation or recent judicial opinion well the status of audit activity by taxing authority change to our estimate of the amount to be realized are recorded in our provision for income tax during the period in which the change occurred we must also ass the likelihood that we will be able to recover our deferred tax asset against future source of taxable income and reduce the carrying amount of deferred tax asset by recording valuation allowance if based on all available evidence it is more likely than not that all or portion of such asset will not be realized this assessment which is completed on taxing jurisdiction basis take into account various type of evidence including the following nature frequency and severity of current and cumulative financial reporting loss pattern of objectively measured recent financial reporting loss is heavily weighted source of negative evidence we generally consider cumulative pre tax loss in the three year period ending with the current quarter to be significant negative evidence regarding future profitability we also consider the strength and trend of earnings well other relevant factor in certain circumstance historical information may not be relevant due to change in our business operation source of future taxable income future reversal of existing temporary difference are heavily weighted source of objectively verifiable positive evidence projection of future taxable income exclusive of reversing temporary difference are source of positive evidence only when the projection are combined with history of recent profit and can be reasonably estimated otherwise these projection are considered inherently subjective and generally will not be sufficient to overcome negative evidence that includes relevant cumulative loss in recent year particularly if the projected future taxable income is dependent on an anticipated turnaround to profitability that ha not yet been achieved in such case we generally give these projection of future taxable income no weight for the purpose of our valuation allowance assessment and tax planning strategy if necessary and available tax planning strategy could be implemented to accelerate taxable amount to utilize expiring carryforwards these strategy would be source of additional positive evidence and depending on their nature could be heavily weighted in assessing the realizability of deferred tax asset we consider the trade offs between cash preservation and cash outlay to preserve tax credit in we reversed million of the previously established valuation allowance the reversal primarily reflects change in our intent to pursue planning action involving cash outlay to preserve tax credit we presently believe that global valuation allowance of billion are required we believe that we ultimately will recover the remaining billion of deferred tax asset however the ultimate realization of our deferred tax asset is subject to number of variable including our future profitability within relevant tax jurisdiction and future tax planning and the related effect on our cash and liquidity position accordingly our valuation allowance may increase or decrease in future period for additional information regarding income tax see for each of the standard is permitted quantitative and qualitative disclosure about market riskoverviewwe are exposed to variety of market and other risk including the effect of change in foreign currency exchange rate commodity price and interest rate well risk to availability of funding source hazard event and specific asset risk these risk affect our automotive and ford credit segment differently we monitor and manage these exposure an integral part of our overall risk management program which includes regular report to central management committee the global risk management committee grmc the grmc is chaired by our chief financial officer and the committee includes our controller and treasurer our automotive and ford credit segment are exposed to liquidity risk including the possibility of having to curtail business or being unable to meet financial obligation they come due because funding source may be reduced or become unavailable our plan is to maintain funding source to ensure liquidity through variety of economic or business cycle discussed in greater detail in item our funding source include sale of receivables in securitizations and other structured financing unsecured debt issuance equity and equity linked issuance and bank borrowing we are exposed to variety of risk such loss or damage to property liability claim and employee injury we protect against these risk through the purchase of commercial insurance that is designed to protect above our self insured retention against event that could generate significant loss direct responsibility for the execution of our market risk management strategy resides with our treasurer office and is governed by written policy and procedure separation of duty is maintained between the development and authorization of derivative trade the transaction of derivative and the settlement of cash flow regular audit are conducted to ensure that appropriate control are in place and that they remain effective in addition our market risk exposure and our use of derivative to manage these exposure are approved by the grmc and reviewed by the audit committee of our board of director in accordance with our corporate risk management policy we use derivative instrument when available such forward contract swap and option that economically hedge certain exposure foreign currency commodity and interest rate we do not use derivative contract for trading market making or speculative purpose in certain instance we forgo hedge accounting and in certain other instance our derivative do not qualify for hedge accounting either situation result in unrealized gain and loss that are recognized in income for additional information on our derivative see note of the note to the financial statement the market and counterparty risk of our automotive and ford credit segment are discussed and quantified below automotive market riskour automotive segment frequently ha expenditure and receipt denominated in foreign currency including the following purchase and sale of finished vehicle and production part debt and other payable subsidiary dividend and investment in foreign operation these expenditure and receipt create exposure to change in exchange rate we also are exposed to change in price of commodity used in the production of our vehicle and change in interest rate foreign currency risk commodity risk and interest rate risk are measured and quantified using model to evaluate the sensitivity of market value to instantaneous parallel shift in rate and or price foreign currency risk foreign currency risk is the possibility that our financial result could be worse than planned because of change in currency exchange rate accordingly our practice is to use derivative instrument to hedge our economic exposure with respect to forecasted revenue and cost asset liability and firm commitment denominated in certain foreign currency consistent with our overall risk management strategy in our hedging action we use derivative instrument commonly used by corporation to reduce foreign exchange risk forward contract quantitative and qualitative disclosure about market risk continued the net fair value of foreign exchange forward contract including adjustment for credit risk of december wa liability of million compared with liability of million of december the potential change in the fair value from change in the underlying exchange rate in dollar term would have been billion at december compared with billion at december the sensitivity analysis presented is hypothetical and assumes foreign exchange rate change are instantaneous and adverse across all currency in reality some of our exposure offset and foreign exchange rate move in different magnitude and at different time and any change in fair value would generally be offset by change in the underlying exposure see note of the note to the financial statement for more information regarding our foreign currency exchange contract commodity price risk commodity price risk is the possibility that our financial result could be worse than planned because of change in the price of commodity used in the production of motor vehicle such base metal steel copper and aluminum precious metal palladium energy natural gas and electricity and plastic resin polypropylene we transition to greater mix of battery electric vehicle we expect to increase our reliance on lithium cobalt and nickel for battery accordingly our practice is to use derivative instrument to hedge the price risk with respect to forecasted purchase of certain commodity that we can economically hedge primarily base metal and precious metal and consistent with our overall risk management strategy in our hedging action we use derivative instrument commonly used by corporation to reduce commodity price risk financially settled forward contract the extent to which we hedge is also impacted by our ability to achieve designated hedge accounting the net fair value of commodity forward contract including adjustment for credit risk of december wa an asset of million compared with an asset of million of december the potential change in the fair value from change in the underlying commodity price would be million at december compared with million at december the sensitivity analysis presented is hypothetical and assumes commodity price change are instantaneous and adverse across all commodity in reality commodity price move in different magnitude and at different time and any change in fair value would generally be offset by change in the underlying exposure in addition our purchasing organization with guidance from the grmc appropriate negotiates contract for the continuous supply of raw material in some case these contract stipulate minimum purchase amount and specific price and therefore play role in managing commodity price risk interest rate risk interest rate risk relates to the loss we could incur in our company cash investment portfolio due to change in interest rate our interest rate sensitivity analysis on the investment portfolio includes cash and cash equivalent and net marketable security at december company cash consisted of billion of rivian marketable security and billion of cash in our investment portfolio compared to billion of company cash at december we invest the portfolio in security of various type and maturity the value of which are subject to fluctuation in interest rate the investment strategy is based on clearly defined risk and liquidity guideline to maintain liquidity minimize risk and earn reasonable return on the short term investment in investing the cash in our investment portfolio safety of principal is the primary objective and risk adjusted return is the secondary objective at any time rise in interest rate could have material adverse impact on the fair value of our portfolio assuming hypothetical increase in interest rate of one percentage point the value of our portfolio would be reduced by million calculated of december this compare to million calculated of december while these are our best estimate of the impact of the specified interest rate scenario actual result could differ from those projected the sensitivity analysis presented assumes interest rate change are instantaneous parallel shift in the yield curve in reality interest rate change of this magnitude are rarely instantaneous or parallel quantitative and qualitative disclosure about market risk continued ford credit market riskmarket risk for ford credit is the possibility that change in interest and currency exchange rate will adversely affect cash flow and economic value interest rate risk generally ford credit asset and the related debt have different re pricing period and consequently respond differently to change in interest rate ford credit asset consist primarily of fixed rate retail financing and operating lease contract and floating rate wholesale receivables fixed rate retail financing and operating lease contract generally require customer to make equal monthly payment over the life of the contract wholesale receivables are originated to finance new and used vehicle held in dealer inventory and generally require dealer to pay floating rate debt consists primarily of short and long term unsecured and securitized debt ford credit term debt instrument are principally fixed rate and require fixed and equal interest payment over the life of the instrument and single principal payment at maturity ford credit interest rate risk management objective is to reduce volatility in it cash flow and volatility in it economic value from change in interest rate based on an established risk tolerance that may vary by market ford credit us economic value sensitivity analysis and re pricing gap analysis to evaluate potential long term effect of change in interest rate it then enters into interest rate swap to convert portion of it floating rate debt to fixed or it fixed rate debt to floating to ensure that ford credit exposure fall within the established tolerance ford credit also us pre tax cash flow sensitivity analysis to monitor the level of near term cash flow exposure the pre tax cash flow sensitivity analysis measure the change in expected cash flow associated with ford credit interest rate sensitive asset liability and derivative financial instrument from hypothetical change in interest rate over twelve month horizon interest rate swap are placed to maintain exposure within approved threshold and the asset liability committee review the re pricing mismatch monthly to provide quantitative measure of the sensitivity of it pre tax cash flow to change in interest rate ford credit us interest rate scenario that assume hypothetical instantaneous increase or decrease of one percentage point in all interest rate across all maturity parallel shift well base case that assumes that all interest rate remain constant at existing level in reality interest rate change are rarely instantaneous or parallel and rate could move more or le than the one percentage point assumed in ford credit analysis result the actual impact to pre tax cash flow could be higher or lower than the result detailed in the table below these interest rate scenario are purely hypothetical and do not represent ford credit view of future interest rate movement under these interest rate scenario ford credit expects more debt and liability than asset to re price in the next twelve month other thing being equal this mean that during period of rising interest rate the interest received on ford credit asset will increase le than the interest paid on ford credit debt thereby initially decreasing ford credit pre tax cash flow during period of falling interest rate ford credit would expect it pre tax cash flow to initially increase ford credit pre tax cash flow sensitivity to interest rate movement is highlighted in different than projected quantitative and qualitative disclosure about market risk continued foreign currency risk ford credit policy is to minimize exposure to change in currency exchange rate to meet funding objective ford credit borrows in variety of currency principally dollar canadian dollar euro sterling and renminbi ford credit face exposure to currency exchange rate if mismatch exists between the currency of receivables and the currency of the debt funding those receivables when possible receivables are funded with debt in the same currency minimizing exposure to exchange rate movement when different currency is used ford credit may use foreign currency swap and foreign currency forward to convert substantially all of it foreign currency debt obligation to the local country currency of the receivables result of this policy ford credit belief it market risk exposure relating to change in currency exchange rate at december is insignificant derivative fair value the net fair value of ford credit derivative financial instrument wa an asset of million and billion at december and respectively transition from libor to alternative reference rateswe and our affiliate including ford credit have been working to transition from the london interbank offered rate libor to alternative reference rate we have developed total company inventory of affected financial instrument and contract have been working to transition legacy contract linked to libor to alternative reference rate and are no longer utilizing libor for new contract counterparty riskcounterparty risk relates to the loss we could incur if an obligor or counterparty defaulted on an investment or derivative contract we enter into master agreement with counterparties that allow netting of certain exposure in order to manage this risk exposure primarily relate to investment in fixed income instrument and derivative contract used for managing interest rate foreign currency exchange rate and commodity price risk we together with ford credit establish exposure limit for each counterparty to minimize risk and provide counterparty diversification our approach to managing counterparty risk is forward looking and proactive allowing to take risk mitigation action before risk become loss exposure limit are established based on our overall risk tolerance which is calculated from counterparty credit rating and market based credit default swap cd spread the exposure limit are lower for smaller and lower rated counterparties counterparties that have relatively higher cd spread and for longer dated exposure our exposure are monitored on regular basis and included in periodic report to our treasurer substantially all of our counterparty exposure are with counterparties that have an investment grade rating investment grade is our guideline for minimum counterparty long term rating item financial statement and supplementary data the report of independent registered public internal control over financial reporting is process designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statement for external purpose in accordance with generally accepted accounting principle company internal control over financial reporting includes those policy and procedure that pertain to the maintenance of record that in reasonable detail accurately and fairly reflect the transaction and disposition of the asset of the company ii provide reasonable assurance that transaction are recorded necessary to permit preparation of financial statement in accordance with generally accepted accounting principle and that receipt and expenditure of the company are being made only in accordance with authorization of management and director of the company and iii provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition use or disposition of the company asset that could have material effect on the financial statement because of it inherent limitation internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatement also projection of any evaluation of effectiveness to future period are subject to the risk that control may become inadequate because of change in condition or that the degree of compliance with the policy or procedure may deteriorate judgment the communication of critical audit matter doe not alter in any way our opinion on the consolidated financial statement taken whole and we are not by communicating the critical audit matter be impaired goodwill impairment testing is also performed following an allocation of goodwill to business to be disposed or change in reporting unit we test for impairment by assessing qualitative factor to determine whether it is more likely than not that the fair value of the indefinite lived intangible asset or the reporting unit allocated the goodwill is le than it carrying amount if the qualitative assessment indicates possible impairment the carrying value of the asset or reporting unit is compared with it fair value fair value is measured relying primarily on the income approach by applying discounted cash flow method the market approach using market value or multiple and or third party valuation we capitalize and amortize our finite lived intangible asset over their estimated useful life the carrying amount of intangible asset and goodwill is reported in other asset in the non current asset section of our consolidated balance sheet intangible asset are comprised primarily change in circumstance indicate the carrying value may not be recoverable event that trigger test for recoverability include material adverse change in projected revenue or expense present cash flow loss combined with history of cash flow loss and forecast that demonstrates significant continuing loss significant negative industry or economic trend current expectation that long lived asset group will be disposed of significantly before the end of it useful life significant adverse change in the manner in which an asset group is used or in it physical condition or when there is change in the asset grouping when triggering event occurs test for recoverability is performed comparing projected undiscounted future cash flow to the carrying value of the asset group if the test for recoverability identifies possible impairment the asset group fair value is measured relying primarily on discounted cash flow method to the extent available we will also consider third party valuation of our long lived asset that were prepared for other business purpose an impairment charge is recognized for the amount by which the carrying value of the asset group exceeds it estimated fair value when an impairment loss is recognized for asset to be held and used the adjusted carrying amount of those asset are depreciated over their remaining useful life for the period presented we fair value hierarchy level input include quoted price for identical instrument and are the most observable level input include quoted price for similar instrument and observable input such interest rate currency exchange rate and yield curve level input include data not observable in the market and reflect management judgment about the assumption market participant would use in pricing the instrumentsfixed income security equity commingled fund derivative financial instrument and alternative asset are remeasured and presented within our consolidated financial statement at fair value on accounting policy continued valuation methodfixed income security fixed income security primarily include government security government agency security corporate bond and asset backed security we generally measure fair value using price obtained from pricing service or quote from dealer that make market in such security pricing method and input to valuation model used by the pricing service depend on the security type asset class where possible fair value are generated using market input including quoted price the closing price in an exchange market bid price the price at which buyer stand ready to purchase and other market information for fixed income security that are not actively traded the pricing service use alternative method to determine fair value for the security including quote for similar fixed income security matrix pricing discounted cash flow using benchmark curve or other factor in certain case when market data are not available we may use broker quote or pricing service that use proprietary pricing model to determine fair value the proprietary model incorporate unobservable input primarily consisting of prepayment curve discount rate default assumption recovery rate yield assumption and credit spread assumption an annual review is performed on the security price received from our pricing service which includes discussion and analysis of the input used by the pricing service to value our security we also compare the price of certain security sold close to the quarter end to the price of the same security at the balance sheet date to ensure the reported fair value is reasonable equity equity security are primarily exchange traded and are valued based on the closing bid official close or last trade pricing on an active exchange if closing price are not available security are valued at the last quoted bid price or may be valued using the last available price security that are thinly traded or delisted are valued using unobservable pricing data commingled fund fixed income and public equity security may each be combined into commingled fund investment most commingled fund are valued to reflect our interest in the fund based on the reported year end net asset value nav derivative financial instrument exchange traded derivative for which market quotation are readily available are valued at the last reported sale price or official closing price reported by an independent pricing service on the primary market or exchange on which they are traded over the counter derivative are not exchange traded and are valued using independent pricing service or industry standard valuation model such discounted cash flow when discounted cash flow model are used projected future cash flow are discounted to present value using market based expectation for interest rate foreign exchange rate commodity price and the contractual term of the derivative instrument the discount rate used is the relevant benchmark interest rate libor sonia plus an adjustment for non performance risk the adjustment reflects the full credit default swap cd spread applied to net exposure by counterparty considering the master netting agreement and any posted collateral we use our counterparty cd spread when we are in net asset position and our own cd spread when we are in net liability position in case when market data are not available we use broker quote and model black scholes to determine fair value this includes situation where there is lack of liquidity for particular currency or commodity or when the instrument is longer dated when broker quote or model are used to determine fair value the derivative is categorized within level of the hierarchy all other derivative are categorized within level alternative asset hedge fund generally hold liquid and readily priced security such public equity exchange traded derivative and corporate bond private equity and real estate investment are le liquid external investment manager typically report valuation reflecting initial cost or updated appraisal which are adjusted for cash flow and realized and unrealized gain loss all alternative asset are valued at the nav provided by the investment sponsor or third party administrator they do not have readily available market quotation valuation may be lagged up to six month the nav will be adjusted for cash flow additional investment or contribution and distribution through year end we may make further adjustment for any known substantive valuation change not reflected in the nav motor company and finance receivables are recorded at the time of origination or purchase at fair value and are subsequently reported at amortized cost net of any allowance for credit loss for all finance receivables ford credit defines past due any payment including principal and interest that is at least day past the contractual due date finance receivables classificationfinance receivables are accounted for held for investment hfi if ford credit ha the intent and ability to hold the receivables for the foreseeable future or until maturity or payoff the determination of intent and ability to hold for the foreseeable future is highly judgmental and requires ford credit to make good faith estimate based on all information available at the time of origination or purchase if ford credit doe not have the intent and ability to hold the receivables then the receivables are classified hf each quarter ford credit make determination of whether it is probable that finance receivables originated or purchased during the quarter will be held for the foreseeable future based on historical receivables sale experience internal forecast and budget well other relevant reliable information available through the date of evaluation for purpose of this determination probable mean at least likely and consistent with the budgeting and forecasting period the foreseeable future mean twelve month ford credit classifies receivables hfi or hf on receivable by receivable basis specific receivables included in off balance sheet sale transaction are generally not identified until the month in which the sale occurs held for investment finance receivables classified hfi are recorded at the time of origination or purchase at fair value and are subsequently reported at amortized cost net of any allowance for credit loss cash flow from finance receivables excluding wholesale and other receivables that were originally classified hfi are recorded an investing activity since gaap requires the statement of cash flow presentation to be based on the original classification of the receivables cash flow from wholesale and other receivables are recorded an operating activity held for sale finance receivables classified hf are carried at the lower of cost or fair value cash flow resulting from the origination or purchase and sale of hf receivables are recorded an operating activity in decrease increase in finance receivables wholesale and other decision ha been made to sell receivables that were originally classified hfi the receivables are reclassified hf and carried at the lower of cost or fair value the valuation adjustment if applicable is recorded in other income loss net to recognize the receivables at the lower of cost or fair value motor company and subsidiariesnotes to the financial financial metric group iii marginal to weak financial metric and group iv poor financial metric including dealer classified uncollectible ford credit generally suspends credit line and extends no further funding to dealer classified in group iv ford credit regularly review the model to confirm the continued business significance and statistical predictability of the model and may make update promptly paying each receivable following the sale of the financed vehicle the frequency of on site vehicle inventory audit depends primarily on the dealer risk rating under ford credit policy on site vehicle inventory audit of low risk dealer are conducted only circumstance warrant on site vehicle inventory audit of higher risk dealer are conducted with increased frequency based primarily on the dealer risk rating but also considering the result of electronic monitoring of the dealer performance including daily payment verification and monthly analysis of the dealer financial statement payoff aged inventory over credit line and delinquency report ford credit typically performs credit review of each dealer annually and more frequently review certain dealer based on the dealer risk rating credit lossesthe allowance for credit loss represents an estimate of the lifetime expected credit loss inherent in finance receivables of the balance sheet date the adequacy of the allowance for credit loss is assessed quarterly adjustment to the allowance for credit loss are made by recording charge to ford credit interest operating and other expense on our consolidated income statement the uncollectible portion of finance receivable is charged to the allowance for credit loss at the earlier of when an account is deemed to be uncollectible or when an account is day delinquent taking into consideration the financial condition of the customer or borrower the value of the collateral recourse to guarantor and other factor charge offs on finance receivables include uncollected amount related to principal interest late fee and other allowable charge recovery on finance receivables previously charged off uncollectible are credited to the allowance for credit loss in the event ford credit repossesses the collateral the receivable is charged off and the collateral is recorded at it estimated fair value le cost to sell and reported in other asset on our consolidated balance sheet consumer portfoliofor consumer receivables that share similar risk characteristic such product type initial credit risk term vintage geography and other relevant factor ford credit estimate the lifetime expected credit loss allowance based on collective assessment using measurement model and management judgment the lifetime expected credit loss for the receivables is determined by applying probability of default and loss given default assumption model to monthly expected exposure then discounting these cash flow to present value using the receivable original effective interest rate or the current effective interest rate for variable rate receivable probability of default model are developed from internal risk scoring model taking into account the expected probability of payment and time to default adjusted for macroeconomic outlook and recent performance the model consider factor such risk evaluation at the time of origination historical trend in credit loss which include the impact of tdrs and the composition and recent performance of the present portfolio including vehicle brand term risk evaluation and new used vehicle the loss given default is the percentage of the expected balance due at default that is not recoverable taking into account the expected collateral value and trend in recovery including key metric such delinquency repossession and bankruptcy monthly exposure are equal to the receivables expected outstanding principal and interest balance the allowance for credit loss incorporates forward looking macroeconomic condition for baseline upturn and downturn scenario three separate credit loss allowance are calculated from these scenario they are then probability weighted to determine the quantitative estimate of the credit loss allowance recognized in the financial statement ford credit us forecast from third party that revert to long term historical average after reasonable and supportable forecasting period which is specific to the particular macroeconomic variable and which varies by market ford credit update the forward looking macroeconomic forecast quarterly if management doe not believe the model reflect lifetime expected credit loss for the portfolio an adjustment is made to reflect management judgment regarding qualitative factor including economic uncertainty observable change in portfolio performance and other relevant factor on an ongoing basis ford credit review it model including macroeconomic factor the selection of macroeconomic scenario and their weighting to ensure they reflect the risk of the portfolio motor company and subsidiariesnotes to the financial statementsnote ford credit finance receivables and allowance for credit loss continued non consumer portfoliodealer financing is evaluated on an individual dealer basis by segmenting dealer by risk characteristic such the amount of the loan the nature of the collateral the financial status of the dealer and any tdr modification to determine if an individual dealer requires specific allowance for credit loss if required the allowance is based on the present value of the expected future cash flow of the dealer receivables discounted at the loan original effective interest rate or the fair value of the collateral adjusted for estimated cost to sell for the remaining dealer financing ford credit estimate an allowance for credit loss on collective basis wholesale loan ford credit estimate the allowance for credit loss for wholesale loan based on historical loss to receivable ltr ratio expected future cash flow and the fair value of collateral for wholesale loan with similar risk characteristic the allowance for credit loss is estimated on collective basis using the ltr model and management judgment the ltr model is based on the most recent year of history an ltr ratio is calculated by dividing credit loss charge offs net of recovery by average net finance receivables excluding unearned interest supplement and allowance for credit loss the average ltr ratio is multiplied by the end of period balance representing the lifetime expected credit loss reserve dealer loan ford credit us weighted average remaining maturity method to estimate the lifetime expected credit loss reserve for dealer loan the loss model is based on the industry wide commercial real estate credit loss adjusted to factor in the historical credit loss for the dealer loan portfolio the expected credit loss is calculated under different macroeconomic scenario that are weighted to provide the total lifetime expected credit loss after establishing the collective and specific allowance for credit loss if management belief the allowance doe not reflect all loss inherent in the portfolio due to change in recent economic trend and condition or other relevant forward looking economic factor an adjustment is made based on management judgment motor company and subsidiariesnotes to the financial statementsnote ford credit payment pension plansnon pension plan asset informationinvestment objective and strategy our investment objective for the plan are to minimize the volatility of the value of our pension asset relative to pension obligation and to ensure asset are sufficient to pay plan benefit our largest non plan united kingdom and canada have similar investment objective to the plan investment strategy and policy for the plan and the largest non plan reflect balance of risk reducing and return seeking consideration the objective of minimizing the volatility of asset relative to obligation is addressed primarily through asset liability matching asset diversification and hedging the fixed income asset allocation match the bond like and long dated nature of the pension obligation asset are broadly diversified within asset class to achieve risk adjusted return that in total lower asset volatility relative to the obligation strategy to address the goal of ensuring sufficient asset to pay benefit include target allocation to broad array of asset class and strategy within asset class that provide adequate return diversification and liquidity motor company and subsidiariesnotes to the financial statementsnote retirement benefit continued derivative are permitted for fixed income investment and public equity manager to use efficient substitute for traditional security and to manage exposure to interest rate and foreign exchange risk interest rate and foreign currency derivative instrument are used for the purpose of hedging change in the fair value of asset that result from interest rate change and currency fluctuation interest rate derivative are also used to adjust portfolio duration derivative may not be used to leverage or to alter the economic exposure to an asset class outside the scope of the mandate an investment manager ha been given alternative investment manager are permitted to employ leverage including through the use of derivative or other tool that may alter economic exposure alternative investment execute diverse strategy that provide exposure to broad range of hedge fund strategy equity investment in private company and investment in private property fund significant concentration of risk significant concentration of risk in our plan asset relate to interest rate growth asset and operating risk in order to minimize asset volatility relative to the obligation the majority of plan asset are allocated to fixed income investment which are exposed to interest rate risk rate increase generally will result in decline in the value of fixed income asset while reducing the present value of the obligation conversely rate decrease generally will increase the value of fixed income asset offsetting the related increase in the obligation in order to ensure asset are sufficient to pay benefit portion of plan asset is allocated to growth asset primarily hedge fund real estate private equity and public equity that are expected over time to earn higher return with more volatility than fixed income investment which more closely match pension obligation within growth asset risk is mitigated by constructing portfolio that is broadly diversified by asset class investment strategy manager style and process operating risk include the risk of inadequate diversification and weak control to mitigate these risk investment are diversified across and within asset class in support of investment objective policy and practice to address operating risk include ongoing manager oversight style adherence team strength firm health and internal risk the primary beneficiary of vie when we have both the power to direct the activity that most significantly impact the entity economic performance and the obligation to absorb loss or the right to claim against our general asset liability recognized result of consolidating these vies do not represent additional claim on our general asset rather they represent claim against the specific asset of limited to matter arising out of alleged defect in our product product warranty governmental regulation relating to safety emission and fuel economy or other matter government incentive tax matter including trade and custom alleged illegal act resulting in fine or penalty financial service employment related matter dealer supplier and other contractual relationship intellectual property right environmental matter shareholder or investor matter and financial reporting matter certain of the pending legal action are or purport to be class action some of the matter involve or may involve claim for compensatory punitive or antitrust or other treble damage in very large amount or demand for field service action environmental remediation program sanction loss of government incentive assessment or other relief which if granted would require very large expenditure the extent of our financial exposure to these matter is difficult to estimate many matter do not specify dollar amount for damage and many others specify only jurisdictional minimum to the extent an amount is asserted our historical experience suggests that in most instance the amount asserted is not reliable indicator of the ultimate outcome we accrue for matter when loss are deemed probable and reasonably estimable in evaluating matter for accrual and disclosure purpose we take into consideration factor such our historical experience with matter of similar nature the specific fact and circumstance asserted the likelihood that we will prevail and the severity of any potential loss we reevaluate and update our accrual matter progress over time for the majority of matter which generally arise out of alleged defect in our product we establish an accrual based on our extensive historical experience with similar matter we do not believe there is reasonably possible outcome materially in excess of our accrual for these matter for the remaining matter where our historical experience with similar matter is of more limited value non pattern matter we evaluate the matter primarily based on the individual fact and circumstance for non pattern matter we evaluate whether there is reasonable possibility of material loss in excess of any accrual that can be estimated our estimate of reasonably possible loss in excess of our accrual for all material matter currently reflects indirect tax and custom matter for which we estimate the aggregate risk to be range of up to about billion an increase of about billion from december primarily reflecting an assessment received in in custom matter noted the litigation process is subject to many uncertainty and the outcome of individual matter is not predictable with assurance our assessment are based on our knowledge and experience but the ultimate outcome of any matter could require payment substantially in excess of the amount that we have accrued and or disclosed motor company and subsidiariesnotes to the financial statementsnote commitment
